NEXT:
  current progress
  The Docker build failed during the pip install step. The error indicates that the requirements.txt file contains a Git repository URL (git+https://github.com/fmi-basel/stork.git@40c68fe) without specifying the package name using the #egg= syntax. This is preventing pip from identifying the package name for the Git-based dependency.
  next step
  Modify the Dockerfile to fix the Git-based package installation by either:
  1. Adding a sed command to fix the requirements.txt before installation to include #egg=stork in the Git URL
  2. Or installing the Git-based packages separately before installing the rest of requirements.txt
  The fix should be added before line 32 where pip install is executed.

  #6 59.40  This PPA contains more recent Python versions packaged for Ubuntu.
  #6 59.40 
  #6 59.40 Disclaimer: there's no guarantee of timely updates in case of security problems or other issues. If you want to use them in a security-or-otherwise-critical environment (say, on a production server), you do so at your own risk.
  #6 59.40 
  #6 59.40 Update Note
  #6 59.40 ===========
  #6 59.40 Please use this repository instead of ppa:fkrull/deadsnakes.
  #6 59.40 
  #6 59.40 Reporting Issues
  #6 59.40 ================
  #6 59.40 
  #6 59.40 Issues can be reported in the master issue tracker at:
  #6 59.40 https://github.com/deadsnakes/issues/issues
  #6 59.40 
  #6 59.40 Supported Ubuntu and Python Versions
  #6 59.40 ====================================
  #6 59.40 
  #6 59.40 - Ubuntu 20.04 (focal) Python3.5 - Python3.7, Python3.9 - Python3.13
  #6 59.40 - Ubuntu 22.04 (jammy) Python3.7 - Python3.9, Python3.11 - Python3.13
  #6 59.40 - Ubuntu 24.04 (noble) Python3.7 - Python3.11, Python3.13
  #6 59.40 - Note: Python2.7 (focal, jammy), Python 3.8 (focal), Python 3.10 (jammy), Python3.12 (noble) are not provided by deadsnakes as upstream ubuntu provides those packages.
  #6 59.40 
  #6 59.40 Why some packages aren't built:
  #6 59.40 - Note: for focal, older python versions require libssl<1.1 so they are not currently built
  #6 59.40 - Note: for jammy and noble, older python versions requre libssl<3 so they are not currently built
  #6 59.40 - If you need these, reach out to asottile to set up a private ppa
  #6 59.40 
  #6 59.40 The packages may also work on other versions of Ubuntu or Debian, but that is not tested or supported.
  #6 59.40 
  #6 59.40 Packages
  #6 59.40 ========
  #6 59.40 
  #6 59.40 The packages provided here are loosely based on the debian upstream packages with some modifications to make them more usable as non-default pythons and on ubuntu.  As such, the packages follow debian's patterns and often do not include a full python distribution with just `apt install python#.#`.  Here is a list of packages that may be useful along with the default install:
  #6 59.40 
  #6 59.40 - `python#.#-dev`: includes development headers for building C extensions
  #6 59.40 - `python#.#-venv`: provides the standard library `venv` module
  #6 59.40 - `python#.#-distutils`: provides the standard library `distutils` module
  #6 59.40 - `python#.#-lib2to3`: provides the `2to3-#.#` utility as well as the standard library `lib2to3` module
  #6 59.40 - `python#.#-gdbm`: provides the standard library `dbm.gnu` module
  #6 59.40 - `python#.#-tk`: provides the standard library `tkinter` module
  #6 59.40 
  #6 59.40 Third-Party Python Modules
  #6 59.40 ==========================
  #6 59.40 
  #6 59.40 Python modules in the official Ubuntu repositories are packaged to work with the Python interpreters from the official repositories. Accordingly, they generally won't work with the Python interpreters from this PPA. As an exception, pure-Python modules for Python 3 will work, but any compiled extension modules won't.
  #6 59.40 
  #6 59.40 To install 3rd-party Python modules, you should use the common Python packaging tools.  For an introduction into the Python packaging ecosystem and its tools, refer to the Python Packaging User Guide:
  #6 59.40 https://packaging.python.org/installing/
  #6 59.40 
  #6 59.40 Sources
  #6 59.40 =======
  #6 59.40 The package sources are available at:
  #6 59.40 https://github.com/deadsnakes/
  #6 59.40

  ENV DEBIAN_FRONTEND=noninteractive

      software-properties-common \

      python3.10 \
      python3.10-venv \
      python3.10-dev \

      && python3.10 -m pip install --upgrade pip setuptools wheel
  COPY requirements.txt .
  RUN sed -i 's|git+https://github.com/fmi-basel/stork.git@40c68fe|git+https://github.com/fmi-basel/stork.git@40c68fe#egg=stork|g' requirements.txt
  RUN python3.10 -m pip install torch torchvision torchaudio --index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu \
      && python3.10 -m pip install -r requirements.txt
  RUN mkdir -p data \
      && mkdir -p output \
      && mkdir -p notebooks \
      && mkdir -p matData \

      && mkdir -p conf/training
  COPY . .
  RUN if [ -f "conf/defaults.yaml" ]; then \
      sed -i 's/device: "cuda"/device: "cpu"/g' conf/defaults.yaml; \
      fi && \
      if [ -f "conf/evaluate.yaml" ]; then \
      sed -i 's/device: "cuda"/device: "cpu"/g' conf/evaluate.yaml; \
      fi && \
      if [ -f "conf/data/data-default.yaml" ]; then \
      sed -i 's|data_dir:.*|data_dir: /home/cc/EnvGym/data/RSNN/data|g' conf/data/data-default.yaml; \
      fi
  RUN echo 'DATA_DIR=/home/cc/EnvGym/data/RSNN/data' > .env \
      && echo 'OUTPUT_DIR=/home/cc/EnvGym/data/RSNN/output' >> .env \
      && echo 'MODEL_DIR=/home/cc/EnvGym/data/RSNN/models' >> .env \
      && echo 'PYTHONPATH=/home/cc/EnvGym/data/RSNN' >> .env \
      && echo 'TORCH_DTYPE=float32' >> .env \
      && echo 'NB_WORKERS=2' >> .env \
      && echo 'PRETRAINED_MODELS_DIR=/home/cc/EnvGym/data/RSNN/pretrained_models' >> .env
  RUN echo 'pytest' > requirements-dev.txt \
      && echo 'jupyter' >> requirements-dev.txt \
